Without knowledge of the nature of plants and trees, we might take only a biased view to serve human needs, ignoring the flaws that need not be mentioned; many already discard such knowledge upon hearing it. Why not entirely revise the "Compendium of Materia Medica," retaining only those medicines that are faultless, potentially fifty to seventy kinds, and use those? The intent in the "Rites of Zhou" for physicians to gather toxic medicines for medical purposes, combined with the anxiety of past emperors regarding the completeness of the compendium, suggests a misunderstanding of this practice. To resolve this confusion, it is essential to discuss ailments in detail. When the nature of ailments is clearly understood, a specific ailment will coincide with specific medicines, even as diseases and medicines vary greatly. Beyond evolution's subtlety in nurturing life, identifying that a certain medicine is effective for a particular ailment, while another might be detrimental, leads to naming conventions. Without discussing ailments, how can we determine the efficacy and toxicity of medicines? It becomes evident that the notions of efficacy and toxicity in relation to medicines differ fundamentally from those related to bodily ailments. Those who are unaware insist on treating medicinal properties as fixed entities, which is quite narrow-minded. Therefore, Chang's discussions on ailments are not without necessity. In ancient times, experts on the platform could make clear predictions, and later generations would follow without fail; accumulating knowledge like a pile of rice, they ensured their earlier work was substantial. Though medicine may seem a minor path, it is no different. Chang, unable to change societal norms, truly desires to use this example to illuminate the mechanisms of diseases, examining what can be used and what cannot.[174p]

　　　　　议病式

　　某年某月某地某人，年纪若干，形之肥瘦长短若何，色之黑白枯润若何，声之清浊长短若何，人之形志苦乐若何；病始何日，初服何药，次后再服何药，某药稍效，某药不效；时下昼夜孰重，寒热孰多；饮食喜恶多寡，二便滑涩有无；脉之三部九候何候独异，二十四脉中何脉独见，何脉兼见；其证或内伤，或外感，或兼内外，或不内外；依经断为何病，其标本先后何在，汗吐下和寒泻温补何施，其药宜用七方中何方，十剂中何剂，五气中何气，五味中何味，以何汤名为加减和合，其效验定于何时。一一详明，务令纤毫不爽。起众信从，允为医门矜式，不必演文可也。　　某年者，年上之干支，治病先明运气也。某月者，治病必本四时也。某地者，辨高卑燥湿，五方异宜也。某龄某形某声某气者，用之合脉，图万全也。[175p]

Discussion on Diagnosing Illness

In a certain year, month, and place, a certain person, of a certain age, possessing a certain physique—whether fat, thin, tall, or short; skin tone—whether black, white, or dry and moist; voice—whether clear, murky, long, or short; and the person's disposition—whether full of hardship or joy; when the illness began, what medicine was initially administered, what subsequent medications were taken, which medicine showed some effect, and which did not; presently, what is the balance between day and night, and the severity of cold and heat; preferences and aversions regarding food, as well as the frequency and quality of bowel movements; the pulses—what is unique in the three positions and nine qualities, what pulse is solely present among the twenty-four, and which pulses are combined; whether the symptoms are due to internal injury, external pathogens, both, or neither; based on the classics, what illness is diagnosed, what are the priorities between symptoms and root causes, what treatments are appropriate for sweating, vomiting, purging, and warming or nourishing—what medicines should be chosen from among the seven categories, which dosage from ten options, which elemental energy from five, which taste from five flavors, and what decoction is suitable for mixture and adjustment, and when should effects be expected. Each aspect must be clearly detailed to ensure no minute detail is overlooked. Such a comprehensive understanding should inspire confidence in others, and can serve as a model within the medical profession without the need for elaborate explanations.

For a certain year, it refers to the heavenly stems and earthly branches, and one must first clarify the nature of the season. For a certain month, diagnosis must align with the four seasons. For a certain place, distinctions between elevation, dryness, and humidity must be made, as well as the differing requirements by direction. For a certain age, physique, voice, and energy, these should correspond accurately to the pulse for totality.[175p]

形志苦乐者，验七情劳逸也。始于何日者，察久近传变也。历问病证药物验否者，以之斟酌己见也。昼夜寒热者，辨气分血分也。饮食二便者，察肠胃乖和也。三部九候何候独异者，推十二经脉受病之所也。二十四脉见何脉者，审阴阳表里，无差忒也。依经断为何病者，名正则言顺，事成如律度也。标本先后何在者，识轻重次第也。汗吐下和寒温补泻何施者，求一定不差之法也。七方，大小缓急奇偶复，乃药之制，不敢滥也。十剂，宣通补泄轻重滑涩燥湿，乃药之宜，不敢泛也。五气中何气，五味中何味者，用药最上之法，寒热温凉平，合之酸辛甘苦咸也。引汤名为加减者，循古不自用也。刻效于何时者，逐段辨之不差，以病之新久，五行定痊期也。若是则医案之在人者，工拙自定，积之数十年，治千万人而不爽也。[176p]

The discernment of suffering and joy in relation to the physical form is to observe the interplay between the seven emotions and the exertions of labor and rest. To understand the origins of ailments, one must examine the changes transmitted over time. Inquire about symptoms, remedies, and their effectiveness to refine one’s own insights. Day and night, the temperature variations can clarify the distinctions between the vital and blood systems. The conditions of food intake and bowel movements indicate the harmony of the stomach and intestines. The examination of the three regions and nine pulses reveals the locations of diseases in the twelve meridians. Observing the appearance of the twenty-four pulses sheds light on the balance of yin and yang, ensuring accuracy. When diagnosing based on the classics, correct naming leads to coherent statements, allowing actions to align with prescribed measures. The priority of the fundamental and the branch suggests an understanding of the relative significance of conditions. The methods of sweating, vomiting, purging, warming, and nourishing must be specific and precise. The differentiation of remedies involves careful selection considering size, urgency, and characteristics, avoiding randomness. The ten prescriptions encompass the suitable applications for circulation, nourishment, and other effects without generalization. Among the five qi, the essence of each flavor must be applied as the highest method in treatment: balancing cold, heat, warmth, coolness, and neutrality with sour, pungent, sweet, bitter, and salty flavors. The term "add and subtract" for decoctions implies adherence to ancient practices rather than personal improvisation. The timing of effects should be precisely delineated, considering the acute versus chronic nature of the illness, with the five elements determining the healing period. Thus, the distribution of medical cases in practice is determined by skill, accumulated over decades, able to treat millions with unwavering precision.[176p]

　　　　日知录 【清　顾炎武】

　　　　　论医

　　古之时，庸医杀人；今之时，庸医不杀人，亦不活人，使其人在不死不活之间，其病日深而卒至于死。夫药有君臣，人有强弱。有君臣则用有多少，有强弱则剂有半倍。多则专，专则其效速；倍则厚，厚则其力深。今之用药者，大抵泛杂而均停，既见之不明，而又治之不勇，病所以不能愈也。而世但以不杀人为贤，岂知古之上医，不能无失。《周礼》医师岁终稽其医事以制其食，十全为上，十失一次之，十失二次之，十失三次之，十失四为下。是十失三四，古人犹用之。而淳于意之对孝文，尚谓时时失之，臣意不能全也。《易》曰：裕父之虫往见吝。[177p]

On Medicine

In ancient times, quack doctors would take lives; in the present, while they do not kill, they also do not save lives, leaving patients caught between not living and not dying, allowing their illnesses to worsen until they eventually die. Medicine has its rulers and subjects, just as people have strengths and weaknesses. With rulers and subjects, the dosage varies; with strengths and weaknesses, the remedy is adjusted accordingly. Too much leads to specialization, and specialization results in quick effects; a greater dose thickens the remedy, deepening its power. However, those who use medicine today tend to mix indiscriminately and prescribe uniformly, failing to discern clearly or treat boldly, which is why illnesses cannot be cured. Yet society regards merely not killing as a sign of virtue, unaware that the great doctors of old could not afford to make mistakes. The "Book of Rites" states that physicians at the end of the year should evaluate their medical practices to determine their sustenance: achieving ten successes is the highest, ten failures once earns a lower rank, and so on. Despite having three or four failures, ancient people still employed such doctors. Even Chunyu Yi, responding to Emperor Xiaowen, noted that mistakes are made from time to time, and it is impossible for ministers to be perfect in their duties. The "I Ching" states: "The insect of abundance comes to see misfortune."[177p]

奈何独取夫裕蛊者？以为其人虽死而不出于我之为。呜呼！此张禹之所以亡汉，李林甫之所以亡唐也。　　《唐书》许引宗言：古之上医，惟是别脉；脉既精别，然后识病。夫病之与药，有正相当者，惟须单用一味，直攻彼病，药力既纯，病即立愈。今人不能别脉，其识病源，以情臆度，多安药味，譬之于猎，未知兔所，多发人马，空地遮围，冀有一人获之，术亦疏矣。假令一药，偶然当病，他味相制，气势不行，所以难差，谅由于此。《后汉书》华佗精于方药，处剂不过数种。夫师之六五，任九二则吉，参以三四则凶。是故官多则乱，将多则败，天下之事亦犹此矣。
[178p]

How can one solely rely on a rich and extravagant treatment? It is believed that even if the individual dies, it does not result from my actions. Alas! This is how Zhang Yu brought about the downfall of Han and how Li Linfu led to the fall of Tang.

According to Xu Yinzong in the "Book of Tang": The great physicians of ancient times focused exclusively on distinguishing pulses; once the pulse was precisely identified, they then recognized the illness. The relationship between illness and medicine is such that there is a correct match—one needs only to use a single remedy that directly targets the illness. When the potency of the medicine is pure, the illness will promptly recover. Nowadays, people cannot distinguish pulses and their understanding of the source of illness is based solely on personal conjecture, often overloading the medicinal flavors, akin to a hunt where one does not know of the rabbit's location, scattering men and horses in vain hopes of capturing one, making the strategy ineffective. Suppose a certain medicine happens to suit the illness; if other flavors interfere, the energy and action are impeded, thus making it difficult to differentiate; this is indeed the reason.

In the "Book of the Later Han," it is said that Hua Tuo excelled in formulas and used only a few types of medicines. A master catalogues six or five, relying on nine or two would predict success, while combining three or four would indicate failure. Therefore, when there are too many officials, there is disorder; when there are too many troops, there is defeat; matters of the world are likewise.[178p]
